  548. # [03:53] <njn> bjacob: what does refgraph do?
  549. # [03:53] * Joins: janv (varga@moz-B6E52297.flarion.as5628.telecom.sk)
  550. # [03:54] * Joins: bz (bzbarsky@moz-C7E1A91E.bstnma.fios.verizon.net)
  551. # [03:54] * ChanServ sets mode: +o bz
  552. # [03:54] * Joins: damons (gnubeard@moz-BCB43F5D.hsd1.ca.comcast.net)
  553. # [03:55] <bjacob> njn: it instruments all strong references (like nsRefPtr) ; it scans the heap to construct a graph where the vertices are heap blocks and the edges are strong references (also knows about weak refs) ; from there it allows you to either manually navigate through the graph, or use built-in algorithms to e.g. find cycles in the graph and compare to cycles known to the cycle collector
  554. # [03:55] <njn> bjacob: is this the one that used to be a valgrind tool?
  555. # [03:55] <bjacob> njn: yes
  556. # [03:57] * Joins: JonathanS (JonathanS@74338381.87D4EDDB.521902B0.IP)
  557. # [03:58] * Joins: nmatsakis (nmatsakis@AAE222A3.FDDA6739.2321E71E.IP)
  558. # [03:58] * Quits: karl (karl@538BABFE.A073F3E.97BBD552.IP) (Ping timeout)
  559. # [03:59] <bjacob> njn: i also plan to make it aware of which vertices are wrapped as JS objects. In this way, as it already knows which edges are known to the CC, we will catch the bugs whereby we fail to CC an edge between JS-wrapped objects (even if there is no cycle at c++ level, that needs to be CC'd in case JS would close the cycle)
